тАШрдорд╣рд┐’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рддреГрддреАрдпрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореН ред рддрд╛рдиреНрд╡реЛ рдирд╛рдо рдкреГрдереЛрдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░ рдЛрд╖рд┐рдГ ред рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрд╛рддреГрддреАрдпреЗ рддреНрд░рдпреЛрджрд╢реА рдЪреЗрддрд┐ рддрд┐рд╕реНрд░реЛрд╜рдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГред рдирд╡рдореНрдпрдХреНрд╖рд░рд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрдпрд╛ рдкрдЩреНрдХреНрддрд┐рд░реНрди рдкрд╛рджреИрдГ ред рдПрдХрд╛рджрд╢реА рдиреНрдпрдЩреНрдХреБрд╕рд╛рд░рд┐рдгреНрдпрд╖реНрдЯрдХрджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢рдХрджреНрд╡реНрдпрд╖реНрдЯрдХрд╡рддреА ред рдкрдЮреНрдЪрджрд╢реА рдкреБрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рджреНрдмреГрд╣рддреНрдпрд╛рджреНрдпрджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢рдХрддреНрд░реНрдпрд╖реНрдЯрдХрд╛ ред рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рдирд╡ рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░рдкрдЩреНрдХреНрддрд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрджрд╕реНрдХрд╛рдГ ред рдЖрджреНрдпреМ рдЬрд╛рдЧрддреМ рджреНрд╡реМ рдЧрд╛рдпрддреНрд░реМ рд╕рд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░рдкрдЩреНрддрд┐рдГрд┐рд╖ ред рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ - рдорд╣рд┐ рддрд╛рдиреНрд╡рдГ рдкрд╛рд░реНрдердГ рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░рдкрд╛рдЩреНрдХреНрддрдВ рдкреБрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рджреНрдмреГрд╣рддреНрдпрдиреНрддрдВ рддреНрд░рдпреЛрджрд╢реНрдпреБрдкрд╛рджреНрдпреЗ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрднреЛ рдирд╡рдореНрдпрдХреНрд╖рд░реИрдГ рдкрдЩреНрдХреНрддрд┐рд░реЗрдХрд╛рджрд╢реА рдиреНрдпрдЩреНрдХреБрд╕рд╛рд░рд┐рдгреА’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЧрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

93 (919)
All Gods
T─Бnva P─Бrtha
15 verses: prast─Бrapaс╣Еkti, except anuс╣гс╣нubh 2тАУ3, 13, paс╣Еkti? 9, nyaс╣Еkus─Бriс╣З─л 11, purast─Бdbr╠еhat─л 15 [per Anukramaс╣З─л]
Even more so than the previous hymn, X.92, this hymn to the All Gods poses more challenges to the interpreter than it yields rewards. This opinion seems to be almost universally shared (see, e.g., Geldner, Renou, Gonda [1975: 212]), and it is generally agreed that some of the problems may be due to faulty transmission.
The poem is composed in a variety of meters, with verses of mixed twelve/ eleven- and eight-syllable p─Бdas, at least in principleтАФthough often these p─Бdas do not conform, by syllable count, caesura, or cadence quantities, to their models. (On the meter see Oldenberg 1888: 101, 117.) The syntax of the hymn is also quite sketchy, with many verbs missing and with nominal forms often apparently merely juxtaposed rather than being linked by normal case relations, and the identity of the referents in many verses is obscure.
The reasons for the choice of the gods honored and their sequence are also not clear. The hymn begins with a verse to Heaven and Earth, who recur in verse 10. Verses 2тАУ3 treat the gods in general, while verse 4 begins to name names, starting with the ─Аdityas. The next three verses (5тАУ7) form a relatively well-organized unit, with a focus on the A┼Ыvins and a shared opening (ut├б naс╕е тАЬand usтАЭ). The end of verse 7 provides a transition to verse 8, with the R╠еbhus and their master, Indra, who also appears in verses 9 and 11. The poet summarizes his poem in verse 12 (with more pride than we would perhaps allow him). Verses 13тАУ15 constitute a d─Бnastuti, mentioning a number of patrons. Note that the name that the Anukramaс╣З─л supplies for the poet has simply been extracted from the name(s) of one or more patrons in verse 15.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHeaven and earth, be great and spacious; mighty Rodas─л, be ever with us like wives; with these (yourprotections), protect us from (the foe who is) stronger (than we), with these protect us in the might (of ourenemies).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Become greatly wide, o Heaven and Earth; the two world-halves are always like exuberant young women for us.
With these (gods?) protect us from one more powerful; with them protect us when (he is) swollen with strength.

Griffith

MIGHTY are ye, and far-extended, Heaven and Earth: both Worlds are evermore to us like two young Dames.
Guard us thereby from stronger foe; guard us hereby to give us strength.

Geldner

Seid recht weit, Himmel und Erde! Immer erscheinen uns die beiden Rodasi wie zwei j├╝ngste Frauen. Mit diesen sch├╝tzet uns vor einem Gewaltigeren, mit ihnen sch├╝tzet uns, um ├╝berlegen zu sein!

Grassmann

O Himmel und Erde, seid uns weit ausgedehnt, o ihr Welten beide, stets wie zwei rastlose Weiber; mit diesen [Helfern] sch├╝tzt uns vor dem st├дrkeren, mit diesen sch├╝tzt uns in unserm Machtbesitz.

What else is Rudra, praised of men? the Maruts, Bhaga, Pusana?

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAnd (you two A┼Ыvins) showering wealth, (you) sun and moon, (lords) of the waters, equally rich,(come) by night to our abode, when Ahirbudhnya sits down in their company in the firmamental (clouds).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

WhenAhirbudhnya: yad = who, referring to Ahirbudhnya

Jamison Brereton

And for us by night (and by day), o you two of bullish goods [=A┼Ыvins], the Sun and Moon are our joint guides toward the seat of the waters, when in company with them Ahi Budhnya [/the Serpent of the Deep] has been set in the depths.

Griffith

Come also to our dwelling, Lords of ample wealth, common partakers of our waters, Sun and Moon,
When the great Dragon of the Deep hath settled down upon their floors.

Geldner

Und bringet uns, ihr beiden Schatzreichen, den Apam Napat, Sonne und Mond als Teilhaber zum Niedersitzen, da├Я in ihrer Gesellschaft sich der Drache der Tiefe in den Tiefen setzen m├╢ge.

Grassmann

Und naht euch ihr beiden stierkr├дftigen Gef├дhrten, Sonne und Mond dem Sitze unserer Gew├дsser [der Somatr├дnke], wenn sich zugleich in ihrem Boden der Drache des Wolkenbodens niedergelassen hat.

рдЙрдд рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рд╢реБрднрд╕реНрдкрддреА рд╢реБрднрд╕реНрдпреЛрджрдХрд╕реНрдп рдкрддреА рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╛ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреМ рджреЗрд╡реМ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдзрд╛рдорднрд┐рдГ рдЖрддреНрдореАрдпреИрдГ рд╢рд░реАрд░реИрдГ рдЙрд░реБрд╖реНрдпрддрд╛рдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рддрд╛рдореН ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд░реБрдгреМ рдЖрддреНрдореАрдпреИрдГ рд╢рд░реАрд░реИрд░реБрд░реБрд╖реНрдпрддрд╛рдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рддрд╛рдореН ред рдпрдВ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдВ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рдордореА рджреЗрд╡рд╛ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддрд┐ рд╕рдГ рдорд╣рдГ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрд┐ рд░рд╛рдпрдГ рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдПрд╖рддреЗ рдЖрднрд┐рдореБрдЦреНрдпреЗрди рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рджреБрд░рд┐рддрд╛ рджреБрд░рд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐ рд╢реАрдШреНрд░рдореН рдЕрддрд┐ рдЕрддрд┐рдЧрдиреНрддрд╛рддрд┐рдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрд╛ рдЪ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рддрддреНрд░ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдГ ред рдзрдиреНрд╡реЗрд╡ ред рдпрдерд╛ рдкрдерд┐рдХреЛ рдирд┐рд░реБрджрдХрд╛рдиреН рджреЗрд╢рд╛рдирддрд┐рдХреНрд░рд╛рдорддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рджрд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAnd may the divine A┼Ыvins, the lords of pure (water), and Mitra and Varuс╣Зa protect us with theirbodies; he (whom they protect) acquires ample riches, (and passes) through misfortunes as (a traveller through)a desert.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

And for us let the two gods, the A┼Ыvins, lords of beauty, let Mitra and Varuс╣Зa make broad space through their domains.
He hastens toward great riches, across difficulties as if across wastelands.

Griffith

And let the Asvins, Lords of splendour, set us free,- both Gods, and, with their Laws, Mitra and Varuna.
Through woes, as over desert lands, he speeds to ample opulence.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe mighty (Indra) is resplendent (through the sacrifice), the joy of the worshipper is resplendent;vigorous are the two horses of you rapidly approaching, whose hymn is unassailable (by the r─Бkс╣гasas); (this)sacrifice is apart, not human.тАЭ

I.e., it is from heaven

Jamison Brereton

Craftsmanly is the Master of the R╠еbhus [=Indra]; craftsmanly is the exhilarating drink of the one who does honorтАФ(let) your two
prizewinning fallow bays (come) hither, as you speedтАФ

Griffith

Prompt is Rbhuksan, prompt the worshipper’s strong drink: may thy fleet Bay Steeds, thine who sperdest on, approach.
Not mans but God’s is sacrifice whose psalm is unassailable.

Geldner

Grassmann

T├╝chtig ist Ribhukschan, t├╝chtig der Rauschtrank des Verehrers; her [m├╢gen kommen] deine, des eilenden, rasche Goldrosse[487] beide, dessen Gesang selbst unbezwinglich ist in herrlicher Weise wie das Opfer der Menschen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMake us, divine Savit─Б, free from shame; you are praised (by the priests) of the opulent; may Indra,accompanied by the bearers (of water), unite the strength of us men here, like the chariot-wheel and reinс╣гтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bearers of water: the Maruts

Jamison Brereton

Make for us immoderation (of wealth), god Savitar. I will praise (you?) in company with our patrons.
Along with his draft-horses, Indra keeps hitching up (wealth) for these (patrons) of ours and keeps hold of тАЬthe wheel of the domainsтАЭ like a rein.

Griffith

O God Savitar, harmed by none, lauded, give us a place among wealthy princes.
With his Car-steeds at once ‘hath our Indra guided the reins and the car of these men.

Geldner

Wirke k├╝hn f├╝r uns, o Gott [savitar ist Glosse, wie das Versmass zeigt], als solcher wirst du gepriesen unter den M├дchtigen; zugleich mit den fahrenden [Maruts?] hat unser Indra dieser M├дnner Rad und Z├╝gel kr├дftig hergelenkt.

English translation:

тАЬHeaven and earth, grant to these our sons great renown, extending over all mankind; grantsustenance for the acquisition of strength, sustenance together with wealth for the overthrow (of enemies).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

On them, o Heaven and Earth, confer great fame reaching to all domains, and on the heroes among us,
(and confer) strengthening nourishment for the winning of the prize, strengthening nourishment for victory through wealth.

Griffith

To these men present here, O Heaven and Earth, to us grant lofty fame extending over all mankind.
Give us a steed to win us strength, a steed with wealth for victory.

Geldner

O Himmel und Erde, verleihet uns, den M├дnnern hier, grossen Reichthum, der zu allen Menschen dringt, ein Ross um Beute zu erlangen, ein Ross mit Gut beladen zum Siege.

English translation:

тАЬMighty Indra, do you, who are well affected towards us, ever protect this worshipper wherever he maybe, so that he may attain his desire; instrumental uct me, Vasu, by your wisdom.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O Indra, inclined toward us, (come?) to this laudation, wherever it may be, for our dominance, mighty one.
Always protect (us) for our dominance. Let our acquisition fatten, o good one.

Griffith

This speaker, Indra-for thou art our Friend-wherever he may be, guard thou, Victor! for help, ever for help
Thy wisdom, Vasu! prosper him.

Geldner

Grassmann

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay (the priests) strengthen this my hymn, the destroyer of the enemies (of the gods), of brilliant pathlike, the rays in the sun, as the carpenter (sends forth) the upright car.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This praise of mine for the superior men, the praise whose course is dazzling as if by its stretching to the sun, they have strengthened,
as a carpenter strengthens a horse-тАЬconciliatorтАЭ [=piece of horse tack?], (so) it cannot be budged.

Griffith

So have they strengthened this mine hymn which seems to take its bright path to the Sun, and reconciles the men:
Thus forms a carpenter the yoke of horses, not to be displaced.

Geldner

Diesen meinen Lobgesang auf die Herren, der von gl├дnzender Auffahrt ist, sollen sie gro├Я, sollen sie stark machen, wie die Tochter des Surya, wie der Zimmermann das Eintrachtsmittel f├╝r Rosse, das unverr├╝ckbare.

Grassmann

Dies mein Lob der M├дnner [der G├╢tter?], das wie in stetigem Laufe auf gl├дnzender Bahn zur Sonne dringt, haben sie wohlbefestigt, wie der Zimmermann ein nicht abzusch├╝ttelndes Joch der Rosse.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThose whose (praise) arrives, accompanied by wealth, of them it is (as) a golden (ornament), likemanly powers in battle reaching the conclusion as it were, without an effort.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

They whose (priestly gift) comes rolling, their (priestly gift) is golden, yoked with wealthтАФ
(it is) like manly forces when facing the other side, like one whose ends have been accomplished [?] at will.

Griffith

Whose chariot-seat hath come again laden with wealth and bright with gold,
Lightly, with piercing ends, as ’twere two ranks of heroes ranged for fight.

Geldner

Deren Daksina mit Reichtum kommt - geschirrt ist ihre goldene Daksina mit ……… Enden wie die Streitkr├дfte im Kampfe, wie das Sch├╢pfrad.

Grassmann

Deren mit Gut beladene goldene Achse, die mit beiden [Enden durch die Naben] geht, rollte wie aus eigner Lust, gleich Heldenscharen in der Schlacht.

English translation:

тАЬThis I proclaim in the presence of Du┼Ы─лma, Pс╣Ыthav─Бna, Vena, the mighty R─Бma, and (other)opulent (princes); those who (come), having yoked five hundred (chariots), their affection for us is renowned onthe road.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I proclaim this in front of Duс╕е┼Ы─лma, Pr╠еthav─Бna, Vena, in front of R─Бma the lordly, in front of the patrons
who, having yoked five hundred, (sent) them along the path, destined for us, (so that) their (priestly gift) has become widely famed.

Griffith

This to Duhsima Prthavana have I sung, to Vena, Rama, to the nobles, and the King.
They yoked five hundred, and their love of us was famed upon their way.

English translation:

тАЬStrongest of them T─Бnva promptly demanded seven and seventy (cows), P─Бrthya demandedall three names may refer to the same person n].тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

In addition here and now seven and seventy
at once did T─Бnva assign (to us), at once did P─Бrthya assign, at once did M─Бyava assign.

Griffith

Besides, they showed us seven -and-seventy horses here.
Tanva at once displayed his gift, Parthya at once displayed his gift; and straightway Mayava showed his.

Geldner

Da wies ├╝berdies noch sieben und siebenzig am gleichen Tage Tanva an, wies am gleichen Tage Parthya an, wies am gleichen Tage Mayava an.

Grassmann

Ausserdem wies uns hier siebenundsiebzig [Rosse] T─Бnua [der Nachkomme des Tanva] sogleich als Geschenk an, sogleich auch P─Бrthia [der Nachkomme des Prithi], sogleich auch M─Бjava [der Nachkomme des Maju].
